# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# gRPC Error Status Propagation Across Go Services

## Your Task

Compare how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated in kubernetes/kubernetes vs grafana/grafana vs etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that create gRPC Status errors with codes (codes.NotFound, codes.Internal, etc.) and the files that translate gRPC errors to HTTP responses.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*


66-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis comparing how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated across the three repositories. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings:

### **etcd-io/etcd**
- **Error Creation:** Centralized in `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` with pre-defined errors using codes like `InvalidArgument`, `NotFound`, `FailedPrecondition`, `Unavailable`, etc.
- **Propagation:** Via `togRPCError()` function in `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go` using a `toGRPCErrorMap` for domain error mapping
- **HTTP Translation:** Uses gRPC gateway in `api/etcdserverpb/gw/rpc.pb.gw.go` with standard `status.Errorf()` calls

### **kubernetes/kubernetes**
- **Error Creation:** Direct creation in various files like `staging/src/k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/cri/streaming/errors.go`
- **HTTP Translation:** Explicit conversion using `WriteError()` function with switch statements, plus vendored grpc-gateway's `HTTPStatusFromCode()` function
- **Gateway Integration:** Uses `vendor/github.com/grpc-ecosystem/grpc-gateway/v2/runtime/` libraries for automatic HTTP status mapping

### **grafana/grafana**
- **Error Creation:** Distributed across interceptors and services in files like `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go`
- **HTTP Translation:** Via `AsErrorResult()` in `pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go` using `runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode()`
- **Custom Handlers:** Uses grpc-gateway with custom error handlers and OpenFGA's `ConvertToEncodedErrorCode()` for specialized mapping

The analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with files, symbols, error chain mappings, and detailed narrative explanations.

The `vendor/github.com/grpc-ecosystem/grpc-gateway/v2/runtime/errors.go` file contains the core `HTTPStatusFromCode()` function (lines 34-38) that converts gRPC codes to HTTP status codes. This function is used in `runtime/handler.go` (line 232) to set HTTP response headers automatically.\\n\\n## grafana/grafana\\n\\nGrafana creates gRPC errors directly in various interceptors and service files. In `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go`, the authenticator creates errors like `status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, ...)` (line 71, 79, 104, 114, 118, 123) and `status.Error(codes.PermissionDenied, ...)` (line 118, 123) for authentication and authorization failures.\\n\\nError translation to HTTP status happens in `pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go`. The `AsErrorResult()` function (lines 122-165) uses `runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode(st.Code())` from grpc-gateway to convert extracted gRPC status codes to HTTP status codes. It also provides helper functions like `NewBadRequestError()` and `NewNotFoundError()` that create errors with specific HTTP status codes.\\n\\nFor the OpenFGA integration in `pkg/services/authz/zanzana/server/openfga_server.go`, Grafana uses custom error handlers (lines 225-234) with `runtime.WithErrorHandler()` that leverages OpenFGA's `serverErrors.ConvertToEncodedErrorCode()` to map gRPC status codes to custom error codes before sending HTTP responses.\\n\\n## Cross-Repository Patterns\\n\\nAll three repositories use `google.golang.org/grpc/status` for creating and handling gRPC Status errors. The key difference in approaches is:\\n\\n1. **etcd** uses centralized error definition and mapping through `toGRPCErrorMap`\\n2. **Kubernetes** uses direct error creation with explicit gRPC-to-HTTP conversion in specific handlers plus grpc-gateway's automatic conversion\\n3. **Grafana** uses distributed error creation with flexible conversion through grpc-gateway's `HTTPStatusFromCode()` and custom error handler plugins\\n\\nThe error code families used across all three repositories include: InvalidArgument, NotFound, FailedPrecondition, Unavailable, ResourceExhausted, OutOfRange, Canceled, DeadlineExceeded, PermissionDenied, Unauthenticated, DataLoss, and Unknown.\"\n}\n",
